# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes RBAC ClusterRole Privilege Escalation Paths

## Your Task

Audit kubernetes/kubernetes for RBAC privilege escalation paths. Find all Go source files that validate ClusterRole escalation rules — specifically, the files that enforce the 'escalation' verb restriction and prevent users from granting permissions they don't hold.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Break every servantRule into individual rule tuples: group, verb, resource, resourceName\n29: \t// 2.  Compare the mini-rules against each owner rule.  Because the breakdown is down to the most atomic level, we're guaranteed that each mini-servant rule will be either fully covered or not covered by a single owner rule\n30: \t// 3.  Any left over mini-rules means that we are not covered and we have a nice list of them.\n31: \t// TODO: it might be nice to collapse the list down into something more human readable\n32: \n33: `pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go`, which defines three critical functions:\\n\\n1. `EscalationAllowed()` - The first line of defense that checks if a user is a superuser (member of system:masters group), which bypasses all escalation checks.\\n\\n2. `RoleEscalationAuthorized()` - Checks if the user has explicit authorization to escalate role resources. This function constructs an authorization request with the verb 'escalate' and queries the authorizer to determine if the user is permitted to escalate.\\n\\n3. `BindingAuthorized()` - Checks if the user is authorized to bind a specific role or clusterrole. For ClusterRoleBindings, this verifies the user can bind the referenced clusterrole across all namespaces. Additionally enforces that aggregationRules can only be set by cluster-admin users.\\n\\n2. `pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go` - Prevents privilege escalation when creating or updating Roles within namespaces.\\n\\n3. `pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go` - Prevents binding to ClusterRoles unless the user already has all permissions in that ClusterRole.\\n\\n4. `pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go` - Prevents binding to Roles unless the user already has all permissions in that Role.\\n\\nAll storage implementations follow a consistent pattern:\\n- Allow superusers (EscalationAllowed)\\n- Allow users with explicit escalate/bind authorization (RoleEscalationAuthorized/BindingAuthorized)\\n- Otherwise, verify via ConfirmNoEscalation that the user's current permissions cover the roles/permissions being granted\\n\\nThe `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/internal_version_adapter.go` file bridges internal and v1 API versions, converting internal PolicyRules before validation.\\n\\nTogether, these components implement a defense-in-depth strategy preventing users from granting RBAC permissions they don't themselves possess, a fundamental principle of the RBAC authorization model.\"\n}\n",
